Union">Croatia and the European Union</a>)</span></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" </tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>2013 enlargement of the European Union</b> saw <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a> join the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> as its 28th <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">member state</a> on 1 July 2013.\n</p><p>The country applied for EU membership in 2003, and the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> recommended making it an official candidate in early 2004. Candidate country status was granted to Croatia by the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a> in mid-2004. The entry negotiations, while originally set for March 2005, began in October that year together with the screening process.\n</p><p>The accession process of Croatia was complicated by the insistence of <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, an EU member state, that the <a href="/wiki/Croatia%E2%80%93Slovenia_border_disputes" title="Croatia\xe2\x80\x93Slovenia border disputes">two countries\' border issues</a> be dealt with prior to Croatia\'s accession to the EU.  Croatian public opinion was generally supportive of the EU accession process, despite occasional spikes in <a href="/wiki/Euroscepticism" title="Euroscepticism">euroscepticism</a>.\n</p><p>Croatia finished accession negotiations on 30 June 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-eu_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eu-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and on 9 December 2011, signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Accession_2011" title="Treaty of Accession 2011">Treaty of Accession</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Croatian_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2012" title="Croatian European Union membership referendum, 2012">referendum on EU accession</a> was held in Croatia on 22 January 2012, with 66% of participants voting in favour of joining the Union.<sup id="cite_ref-Dw-world.de_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dw-world.de-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-referendum1_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-referendum1-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-referendum2_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-referendum2-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-referendum3_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-referendum3-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>  The ratification process was concluded on 21 June 2013, and entry into force and accession of Croatia to the EU took place on 1 July 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Judicial reform and human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Accession requirements included: judicial reform to strengthen the independence, accountability, impartiality, professionalism and efficiency of the judiciary; a crackdown on corruption and organised crime (this resulted in the conviction of former Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Ivo_Sanader" title="Ivo Sanader">Ivo Sanader</a> for taking bribes); strengthen the protection of minorities; settle outstanding refugee return issues; improve the protection of human rights.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Co-operation_with_the_International_Criminal_Tribunal_for_the_former_Yugoslavia">Co-operation with the International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Co-operation with the International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Croatia had to extradite several of its citizens to the <a href="/wiki/International_Criminal_Tribunal_for_the_Former_Yugoslavia" class="mw-redirect" title="International Criminal Tribunal for the Former Yugoslavia">International Criminal Tribunal for the Former Yugoslavia</a> (ICTY), a United Nations body, an issue that was often contentious in domestic politics. Croatia\'s relations with the ICTY had continually been cited by the EU officials as something that required further improvement. Ratification of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Association_Agreement" title="European Union Association Agreement">EU Stabilisation and Association Agreement</a> with Croatia had been stalled because of this.\n</p><p>The European Council, after its summit of 20 December 2004, set the following 17 March as the date to start entry negotiations, provided that Croatia continued to co-operate fully with the ICTY. On 16 March 2005, the day before talks were to begin, the EU postponed the commencement of negotiations, because the ICTY prosecution assessed the Croatian efforts to capture the fugitive general <a href="/wiki/Ante_Gotovina" title="Ante Gotovina">Ante Gotovina</a> (indicted by the ICTY for <a href="/wiki/War_crimes" class="mw-redirect" title="War crimes">war crimes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity" title="Crimes against humanity">crimes against humanity</a>, but at large since 2001) as neither timely nor sufficient.\n</p><p>On 7 December 2005, the Spanish police finally arrested Ante Gotovina with the help of the Croatian government on the Spanish island of <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a>, located in the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a>. He was brought to <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a> to be tried for war crimes. With the arrest of Ante Gotovina this issue was resolved, and entry negotiations began anew, after the certification of ICTY chief prosecutor <a href="/wiki/Carla_Del_Ponte" title="Carla Del Ponte">Carla Del Ponte</a> that Croatia now fully cooperated with the ICTY.\n</p><p>In April 2011, Croatian generals Gotovina and <a href="/wiki/Mladen_Marka%C4%8D" title="Mladen Marka\xc4\x8d">Marka\xc4\x8d</a> were given extended prison sentences at the ICTY, which was widely perceived as unjust in the Croatian public. This caused a marked increase in opposition to the accession because, in the past, some countries like the Netherlands,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> conditioned their support for the Croatia\'s accession process with the continued Croatian co-operation with the ICTY.\n</p><p>On 16 November 2012, the ICTY Appeals Chamber acquitted generals Gotovina and Marka\xc4\x8d and ordered their immediate release.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Border_disagreements">Border disagreements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Border disagreements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Croatia%E2%80%93Slovenia_border_disputes" title="Croatia\xe2\x80\x93Slovenia border disputes">Croatia\xe2\x80\x93Slovenia border disputes</a></div>\n<p>Croatia has had long-standing border issues with Slovenia, especially over the <a href="/wiki/Piran_Bay" class="mw-redirect" title="Piran Bay">Piran Bay</a> boundary. Between December 2008 and September\xe2\x80\x93October 2009, Slovenia blocked Croatia\'s EU accession over these border issues. On 6 June 2010, Slovenia voted to accept the ruling of United Nation arbitrators on the dispute, removing this obstacle.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Croatia has border disputes with Serbia, Bosnia and Herzegovina, and Montenegro, but these countries are not European Union members and cannot directly block the accession process. In December 2008, Croatia and Montenegro agreed that the outstanding sea border issue between the two countries should be settled before an international court whose decision would be accepted in advance by the parliaments of the two countries.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Land_ownership">Land ownership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Land ownership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Free acquisition of real estate by foreigners is a sensitive issue in Croatia. This matter particularly concerns Italians, especially in <a href="/wiki/Istria" title="Istria">Istria</a>. While it has some ties with Italy, the events surrounding World War II, when Istria changed hands between the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy_(1861%E2%80%931946)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Italy (1861\xe2\x80\x931946)">Kingdom of Italy</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia</a>, remain pertinent. Numerous Italian politicians expressed their discontent concerning the inability of Italians to purchase land in Croatia, considering it discriminatory treatment and stating that the issue should be resolved as soon as possible.\n</p><p>Croatia subsequently denied any discrimination, and said that Croatian legislation provided for the same treatment of all EU citizens concerning land ownership. In mid-2006, Croatia and Italy came to an agreement allowing Italian citizens to purchase land in Croatia and Croatian citizens to purchase land in Italy. Other EU members had to resolve similar issues before their accession to the EU. Examples of this include <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, Slovakia, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, and especially <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shipyard_privatisation">Shipyard privatisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Shipyard privatisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Croatia was required to stop subsidising its shipbuilding industry, resulting in privatisations, closures and reduced production capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Negotiation_progress">Negotiation progress</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Negotiation progress">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Croatia applied for EU membership in 2003, and the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> recommended making it an official candidate in early 2004. Candidate country status was granted to Croatia by the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a> (the EU\'s heads of state and/or government) in mid-2004, but the date for the beginning of entry negotiations, while originally set for March 2005, was put off. In early March 2005, Croatia was formally warned by the EU that its failure to arrest the war crimes suspect <a href="/wiki/Ante_Gotovina" title="Ante Gotovina">Ante Gotovina</a> would jeopardise the country\'s chances of starting the accession talks, in spite of Croatia insisting it was doing everything it could to find and arrest the fugitive<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> and claiming that Gotovina was no longer in Croatia.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In fact, the talks started in October 2005, shortly before Gotovina\'s arrest in <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, which occurred in early December that year and was hailed by the EU as an important turning point for the whole region, as it turned "the page from the nationalist past to a European future".<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Before the start of negotiations with Croatia, the <i><a href="/wiki/Community_acquis" class="mw-redirect" title="Community acquis">acquis</a></i> was divided into 35 chapters, 4 more than the usual 31; the new chapters, previously part of the agricultural policy, are areas expected to be troublesome, as they were with the other applicants. Following the opening of accession negotiations on 3 October 2005, the process of screening 35 acquis chapters with Croatia was completed on 18 October 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Negotiations had been restrained for ten months because of a <a href="/wiki/Croatia%E2%80%93Slovenia_border_disputes" title="Croatia\xe2\x80\x93Slovenia border disputes">border dispute between Croatia and Slovenia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In September 2009 it was announced that Slovenia would remove restraints on Croatia\'s negotiations with the EU without prejudice to the international mediation on the border dispute.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align:left">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th><a href="/wiki/Acquis#Chapters" class="mw-redirect" title="Acquis">Acquis chapter</a></th>\n<th>EC assessment at start</th>\n<th>Current situation\n</th>\n<th style="width:70px;">Screening started\n</th>\n<th style="width:70px;">Screening completed\n</th>\n<th style="width:70px;">Chapter frozen\n</th>\n<th style="width:70px;">Chapter unfrozen\n</th>\n<th style="width:70px;">Chapter opened\n</th>\n<th style="width:70px;">Chapter closed\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">1. id="cite_ref-consilium_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-consilium-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2013-07-01</td>\n<td>Croatia joins the EU.\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Date_of_accession">Date of accession</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Date of accession">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Originally Croatia had been aiming for a 2007 accession date, which would have broken <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>\'s record of 2.5 years of negotiations to complete the process. However, negotiations turned out to be tougher than expected. On 5 November 2008, the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>\'s annual progress report on Croatia\'s candidacy was published. <a href="/wiki/Olli_Rehn" title="Olli Rehn">Olli Rehn</a> stated that the country should aim to complete accession negotiations by the end of 2009, with membership following by 2011 at the latest.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> In 2009 it was also reported that <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> may be fast-tracked into the European Union,<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> and Rehn said that "the EU prefers two countries joining at the same time rather than individually. If Iceland applies shortly and the negotiations are rapid, Croatia and Iceland could join the EU in parallel". The last non-acquis hurdle to membership, the <a href="/wiki/Croatia%E2%80%93Slovenia_border_disputes" title="Croatia\xe2\x80\x93Slovenia border disputes">maritime border dispute with Slovenia</a>, was overcome in November 2009.\n</p><p>Croatia ultimately finished its accession negotiations on 30 June 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-close4prop_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-close4prop-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> and signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Accession_2011" title="Treaty of Accession 2011">Treaty of Accession 2011</a> in Brussels on 9 December 2011; followed by approval of it by a national referendum on 22 January 2012 and completing their ratification process on 4 April 2012. Entry into force and accession of Croatia to the EU took place on <b>1 July 2013</b>, as all 27 EU members and Croatia have <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Accession_2011#Ratification" title="Treaty of Accession 2011">ratified the treaty</a> before this date.<sup id="cite_ref-Ratification_of_Accession_Treaty_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ratification_of_Accession_Treaty-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ratification_Process_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ratification_Process-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The accession took place at a time of economic difficulty with Croatia in a fifth year of recession with 21% unemployment, and amid the <a href="/wiki/European_sovereign-debt_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="European sovereign-debt crisis">European sovereign-debt crisis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As Croatia joined the EU, it exited the <a href="/wiki/Central_European_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Central European Free Trade Agreement">Central European Free Trade Agreement</a> (CEFTA).\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Remaining_areas_of_inclusion">Remaining areas of inclusion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Remaining areas of inclusion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Croatia became a member on 1 July 2013, but some areas of cooperation in the European Union will apply to Croatia at a later date. These are:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_movement_for_workers_in_the_European_Union" title="Freedom of movement for workers in the European Union">Freedom of movement for workers in the European Union</a>, seven year transition period. (Restrictions expire 1 July 2020)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area#Prospective_members" title="Schengen Area">Enlargement of the Schengen Area</a>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_eurozone" title="Enlargement of the eurozone">Enlargement of the eurozone</a>)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Passports_of_the_European_Union" title="Passports of the European Union">Passports of the European Union</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Croatian_passport" title="Croatian passport">Croatian passport</a> still does not follow the EU common passport design with burgundy coloured covers)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area" title="European Economic Area">European Economic Area</a> (see <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area#New_EU_member_states" title="European Economic Area">Enlargement of the European Economic Area</a>)</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Free_movement_of_persons_and_visa_policy">Free movement of persons and visa policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Free movement of persons and visa policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-accession_entry_arrangements_for_Croatian_nationals_travelling_to_EU_member_states">Pre-accession entry arrangements for Croatian nationals travelling to EU member states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Pre-accession entry arrangements for Croatian nationals travelling to EU member states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Before accession to the European Union, Croatia was categorised as an <a href="/wiki/Visa_policy_of_the_European_Union#Visa_exemptions" class="mw-redirect" title="Visa policy of the European Union">Annex II</a> country, which meant that Croatian citizens could stay in the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a> without a visa for up to 90 days in a 180-day period. Croatian citizens were also able to stay without a visa in <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> for up to 90 days in each country, as well as in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> for up to 6 months.\n</p><p>The general rule was that non-EU citizens had to use a passport to enter EU member states. However, there was an exception to the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Agreement" title="Schengen Agreement">Schengen Agreement</a> rules for Croatian citizens. Based on the pre-Schengen bilateral agreements between Croatia and neighbouring EU countries (<a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>), Croatian citizens were allowed to cross the border with only a Croatian national identity card (a passport was not obligatory).<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Many people living near the border crossed it several times a day (some work across the border, or own land on the other side of the border), especially on the border with Slovenia, which was unmarked for centuries as Croatia and Slovenia were both part of the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Habsburg Empire</a> (1527\xe2\x80\x931918) and <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a> (1918\xe2\x80\x931991). Prior to Croatia\'s accession to the EU on 1 July 2013, an interim solution, which received permission from the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>, was found: every Croatian citizen was allowed to cross the Schengen border into Hungary, Italy or Slovenia with an ID card and a special border card that was issued by Croatian police at border exit control. The police authorities of Hungary, Italy or Slovenia would then stamp the special border card both on entry and exit. Croatian citizens, however, were not allowed to enter any other <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Agreement" title="Schengen Agreement">Schengen Agreement</a> countries without a valid passport, although they were allowed to travel between <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>, Italy and Slovenia.\n</p><p>These arrangements were discontinued on 1 July 2013 when Croatia became an EU member state. Since then, Croatian citizens have been able to enter any EU member state using only an <a href="/wiki/Croatian_ID_card" class="mw-redirect" title="Croatian ID card">ID card</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-accession_access_to_free_movement_in_other_EU_member_states">Post-accession access to free movement in other EU member states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Post-accession access to free movement in other EU member states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Citizens%E2%80%99_Rights_Directive" title="Citizens\xe2\x80\x99 Rights Directive">Citizens\xe2\x80\x99 Rights Directive</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_movement_for_workers_in_the_European_Union" title="Freedom of movement for workers in the European Union">Freedom of movement for workers in the European Union</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Croatia_EU_Freedom_of_Movement.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Croatia_EU_Freedom_of_Movement.svg/220px-Croatia_EU_Freedom_of_Movement.svg.png" width="220" height="186" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Croatia_EU_Freedom_of_Movement.svg/330px-Croatia_EU_Freedom_of_Movement.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Croatia_EU_Freedom_of_Movement.svg/440px-Croatia_EU_Freedom_of_Movement.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="432" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Croatia_EU_Freedom_of_Movement.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><b>Freedom of movement of Croatian citizens within EU/EEA/CH</b> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0071BC; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Croatia</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #009245; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;EU member states with free labour market access for Croatian citizens since accession</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #22B573; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other EEA member states with free labour market access for Croatian citizens</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #C1272D; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;EU member states with labour market restrictions for Croatian citizens at least until 1 July 2018</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #F15A24; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Switzerland and Liechtenstein impose permanent labour market restrictions for Croatian citizens</div></div></div></div>\n<p>On 1 July 2013, Croatian nationals became European Union citizens and acquired the <a href="/wiki/Directive_2004/38/EC_on_the_right_to_move_and_reside_freely" class="mw-redirect" title="Directive 2004/38/EC on the right to move and reside freely">right to move and reside freely</a> in other EU member states, as well as in Iceland, Liechtenstein, Norway and Switzerland. On the same day, 14 EU member states (Bulgaria, Czech Republic, Denmark, Estonia, Finland, Hungary, Ireland, Latvia, Lithuania, Poland, Portugal, Romania, Slovakia and Sweden) allowed Croatian nationals to work without restrictions in their country. However, 13 other EU member states imposed transitional restrictions on Croatian nationals wishing to access their labour markets.<sup id="cite_ref-europa.eu_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-europa.eu-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Annex V of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Accession_2011" title="Treaty of Accession 2011">Treaty concerning the accession of the Republic of Croatia to the European Union</a> allows member states to apply national measures regulating Croatian nationals\xe2\x80\x99 access to their labour markets for a period of up to five years, and in case of serious disturbance to their labour markets or the threat thereof, and after notifying the Commission, for a further two years (i.e. up to a maximum of seven years in total).\n</p><p>Croatian nationals who on 1 July 2013 had already resided in an EU member state for a continuous period of at least 5 years acquired the right of <b>permanent residence</b> (meaning that they could work without any restrictions in their host EU member state), as long as during their continuous residence of 5 years they were a worker, self-employed person, self-sufficient person, student or family member accompanying or joining an EU/EEA/Swiss citizen.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 1 July 2013, non-EU/EEA/Swiss citizens who were family members of a Croatian national and accompanying or joining him/her also acquired the <a href="/wiki/Directive_2004/38/EC_on_the_right_to_move_and_reside_freely" class="mw-redirect" title="Directive 2004/38/EC on the right to move and reside freely">right to move and reside freely</a> in other EU member states.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable toccolours" style="border-collapse:collapse" cellpadding="3" border="1">\n<caption><b>Establishment of rights of EU nationals of Croatia to work in another EU member state</b><sup id="cite_ref-europa.eu_63-1" id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Belgium</td>\n<td>1 July 2015<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a 2015\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Malta</td>\n<td>26 January 2018<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Slovenia</td>\n<td>1 July 2018<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Austria</td>\n<td>1 July 2020\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>United Kingdom</td>\n<td>1 July 2018\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Netherlands</td>\n<td>1 July 2018<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Visa_policy_for_third-country_nationals">Visa policy for third-country nationals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Visa policy for third-country nationals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Visa_policy_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Visa policy of the European Union">Visa policy of the European Union</a></div>\n<p>In the run up to accession to the European Union, Croatia aligned its visa policy with that of the European Union. As a result of the new visa regime, some third-country nationals (such as Russian and Turkish nationals) who were previously temporarily exempt from having to obtain a visa to visit Croatia were now subject to a visa requirement. However, to mitigate the effect of the re-imposition of a visa regime on tourist numbers, the Croatian government has introduced a \'facilitated entry of aliens\' procedure, exempting travellers who have a Schengen visa or residence permit from having to obtain an additional Croatian visa to visit Croatia until 31 December 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> In addition, the Croatian government has extended the working hours and capacity of its foreign missions in countries such as Russia and Ukraine to ensure that applications for Croatian visas are processed more efficiently.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Visa_requirements_for_Croatian_nationals_visiting_third_countries">Visa requirements for Croatian nationals visiting third countries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Visa requirements for Croatian nationals visiting third countries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Visa_requirements_for_Croatian_citizens" title="Visa requirements for Croatian citizens">Visa requirements for Croatian citizens</a></div>\n<p>Upon Croatia\'s accession to the European Union on 1 July 2013, several countries and territories outside the European Union aligned the visa requirements imposed on Croatian citizens with those imposed on other EU citizens. For example, on 1 July 2013, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_SAR" class="mw-redirect" title="Hong Kong SAR">Hong Kong SAR</a> extended the visa-free period of stay for Croatian citizens from 14 days to 90 days in line with the visa-free period of stay granted to other EU citizens,<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> whilst <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> introduced a 90-day visa exemption for Croatian citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> It is likely that these countries and territories amended their visa policy for Croatian citizens because of the European Union\'s <a href="/wiki/Visa_policy_of_the_European_Union#Reciprocity" class="mw-redirect" title="Visa policy of the European Union">visa reciprocity mechanism</a>. However, other countries such as <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>  and the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> have not amended their visa policies to harmonise their treatment of Croatian citizens and other EU citizens.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Membership_of_the_Schengen_Area">Membership of the Schengen Area</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Membership of the Schengen Area">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>During June 2011 Croatia began with implementation of the projects and reforms required to join the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a> by 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> By joining the Schengen Area, border checks will be eliminated at the land border with <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, as well as at airports and ports for flights and ships to/from Schengen member states, thus facilitating the freer movement of persons between Croatia and the rest of the Schengen Area.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Membership_of_the_European_Economic_Area">Membership of the European Economic Area</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Membership of the European Economic Area">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area#Future_enlargement" title="European Economic Area">European Economic Area \xc2\xa7&#160;Future enlargement</a></div>\n<p>Croatia\'s accession to the EU obliges them to apply for membership in the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area" title="European Economic Area">European Economic Area</a> (EEA).<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>  The Croatian government submitted their application on 13 September 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> and membership negotiations started 15 March 2013 with the aim to enlarge both the EU and the EEA on the same date, 1 July 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>  However, this was not achieved.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>  On 11 April 2014, the EU and its member states (including Croatia), Norway, Iceland and Liechtenstein signed an agreement concerning the accession of Croatia to the EEA. It is yet to be ratified, but is provisionally applied with regards to Croatia. As of June 2017, the agreement has been ratified by 17 out of 32 parties.\n<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_opinion">Public opinion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Public opinion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Croatian_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2012#Opinion_polls" title="Croatian European Union membership referendum, 2012">Croatian European Union membership referendum, 2012 \xc2\xa7&#160;Opinion polls</a></div>\n<p>Croatian <a href="/wiki/Public_opinion" title="Public opinion">public opinion</a> was divided on EU accession. <a href="/wiki/Croatian_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2012#Opinion_polls" title="Croatian European Union membership referendum, 2012">Opinion polling for the EU referendum</a> showed the population was mostly in favour of joining. Public support ranged from a high of 80% to lows of 26\xe2\x80\x9338%.<sup id="cite_ref-range_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-range-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Political analyst Vi\xc5\xa1eslav Raos cited the <a href="/wiki/2010_European_sovereign_debt_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 European sovereign debt crisis">economic problems within the EU</a> among the factors: "[Croatians] know that the European Union is not a remedy to all economic and social problems. So the EU itself is in a sort of crisis, and that reflects on Croatia\'s accession."<sup id="cite_ref-range_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-range-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> The government announced an information campaign to reverse the drop in support.<sup id="cite_ref-range_86-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-range-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A referendum was held in Croatia on 22 January 2012 on joining the European Union, and the result was 66% approval to join, though the turnout was low at 43.51%.<sup id="cite_ref-Dw-world.de_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dw-world.de-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-referendum1_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-referendum1-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-referendum2_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-referendum2-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-referendum3_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-referendum3-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2013_enlargement_of_the_European_Union&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Croatia_and_the_euro" title="Croatia and the euro">Croatia and the euro</a></li>\n<li><a The ECJ held that periods of residence completed by a national of a non-Member State before the accession of that State to the EU must be taken into account when calculating the five year qualifying period for permanent residence, provided that the conditions laid down in Article 7(1) of Directive 2004/38/EC are satisfied.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-65"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-65">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.bundesregierung.de/Content/EN/Artikel/2015/06_en/2015-06-17-arbeitnehmerfreizuegigkeit-kroatien_en.html">"Federal Government - Labour market open to Croats"</a>. <i>www.bundesregierung.de</i><span class="reference-accessdate">.
